## Section 001: Rust Backend Playbook Reference
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title promises a backend playbook but the seed never states the playbook's organizing claim, the 81-line mapped file structures every service as five layers, transport, handler, domain, persistence, and integration, each narrow enough that failures have an obvious owner
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the five layers exist to give every failure an owner, parsing failures belong to transport, orchestration and error mapping to handlers, invariants to domain types, transactions to persistence, and remote-system risk to typed clients, so debugging becomes a routing problem instead of a search
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: reading the playbook as framework advice misses its point, actix-web, axum, tokio, sqlx, and reqwest appear only as representative ecosystem examples, the layer boundaries are the doctrine and survive any crate swap
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference governs Rust HTTP backend service shape, the parent skill's guardrails route generic Rust libraries, CLIs, parsers, and FFI work to rust-executable-specs-01 or rust-coder-02 instead
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the five-layer anatomy and its failure-ownership rationale so readers know the playbook is a boundary discipline, not a crate catalog
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the playbook is the anatomy volume of a four-reference bundle, testing, runtime-ops, and security-resilience each elaborate one region of the same five-layer body, which is why the reference map routes every task type through the playbook eventually
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat every backend request path as the five named layers, keep each narrow, and decide inline-versus-worker before coding long-running paths
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the five layers exist to give every failure an owner, parsing failures belong to transport, orchestration and error mapping to handlers, invariants to domain types, transactions to persistence, and remote-system risk to typed clients, so debugging becomes a routing problem instead of a search
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; reading the playbook as framework advice misses its point, actix-web, axum, tokio, sqlx, and reqwest appear only as representative ecosystem examples, the layer boundaries are the doctrine and survive any crate swap
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference governs Rust HTTP backend service shape, the parent skill's guardrails route generic Rust libraries, CLIs, parsers, and FFI work to rust-executable-specs-01 or rust-coder-02 instead
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open with the five-layer anatomy and its failure-ownership rationale so readers know the playbook is a boundary discipline, not a crate catalog
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Rust Backend Playbook Reference", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the playbook is the anatomy volume of a four-reference bundle, testing, runtime-ops, and security-resilience each elaborate one region of the same five-layer body, which is why the reference map routes every task type through the playbook eventually

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table maps one local row and four external rows, but the single local file is one chapter of a five-file bundle whose SKILL.md, reference map, and three sibling references carry the modes, testing, operations, and security guidance this theme repeatedly needs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the seed's mapping scoped only the playbook file, so claims about modes, harnesses, migrations, or idempotency must cite the sibling files by name rather than lean on the one mapped row
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: citing the playbook row for a claim that actually lives in a sibling file, spawned-app harnesses or zero-downtime migrations, misattributes evidence even though the bundle is one lineage
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table records provenance for this document's claims, it does not certify that the four GitHub and docs.rs URLs resolve or describe current crate behavior
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the playbook as the mapped anchor row and name the four sibling bundle files explicitly wherever their content is used
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the one-row local map understates the theme by four files, which the seed's own hierarchy confidence warning almost admits, this evolution treats the bundle as context while honoring the single mapped anchor

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed supplies only the corpus document verifier while the bundle defines a real gate stack, format, lint, tests, and build as the CI minimum, integration-first coverage through a spawned-app harness, HTTP mock tests with wiremock, and migration-aware tests when schema changes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the testing sibling argues integration tests catch wiring, serialization, routing, and state-setup errors that unit tests structurally miss, so the gate mix is ordered by what each layer can see, not by execution speed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: gates that stop at cargo test with unit coverage certify the layer backends break least, the expensive failures live at wiring, persistence, and remote boundaries that only harness and mock tests exercise

- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to import the gate stack, CI four-gate minimum, spawned-app integration tests on endpoints, wiremock contract tests on clients, property tests on domain constructors, and migration tests when schema moves

## Section 013: Theme Specific Artifact
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names a request lifecycle diagram with persistence boundary, observability hook, and failure table but gives only generic completion rules, while the playbook supplies the concrete anatomy the diagram must trace
- **supporting_reason:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the diagram's spine is the five-layer path, transport, handler, domain, persistence, integration, its persistence boundary marks the transaction owner, its observability hook carries the correlation identifier the ops sibling requires, and its failure table classifies each layer's failure classes per the security sibling
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a lifecycle diagram without the worker split marked misleads exactly where the architecture decision matters, the inline-versus-durable fork is the diagram's highest-value edge

- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as the five-layer path with the transaction owner, correlation hook, worker fork, and per-layer failure classes annotated

## Section 014: Worked Example Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed describes usage abstractly while the bundle implies one composed walkthrough, a new endpoint that parses at transport, converts to a newtype at the edge, owns one transaction, calls a typed remote client, and proves itself through a spawned-app test with a wiremock contract
- **supporting_reason:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the walkthrough chains five playbook rules and two sibling disciplines into one artifact, so a learner who completes it has exercised the theme's whole boundary doctrine rather than isolated fragments
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: rules taught in isolation lose the composition, a learner who can write a newtype and a handler separately still lets the transaction span the remote call when assembling a real workflow
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: worked examples here teach service anatomy and boundary discipline, deep auth, migration, and worker examples belong to the sibling files' own material
- **revision_decision:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to anchor the section on the composed endpoint walkthrough plus one deliberate failure case, the remote call timing out after the durable intent is saved
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 014 "Worked Example Set", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the playbook's REQ-WEB note makes examples self-verifying, invalid input paths become named contracts with named tests, so a trainee's walkthrough is graded by whether its empty, malformed, and duplicate cases each carry a test
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed names a compile-and-review leading indicator but no loop connects shipped services back to the doctrine, nothing counts which boundary rules recur as review rejections, which incidents trace to unowned layers, or which retries duplicated side-effects
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because review rejections and incidents are each classifiable against the playbook's layer rules and the siblings' risk rules, so tallying them per rule shows which boundaries the team has absorbed and which it re-learns per outage
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: measuring only delivery speed rewards the deferred-cost failures this theme targets, an inline remote call demos faster than a worker split right up to the first duplicated payment

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed budgets one service boundary, 25 endpoints, and 1000 representative requests per review batch, but never connects the budget to the bundle's own unit of work, the mode-classified service slice with its layer boundaries and verification matrix
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the bundle's costs are per-slice, requirements and boundary design are one-time costs per endpoint, the harness amortizes across every integration test, migration sequencing is per-schema-change, and the verification matrix is the recurring cost that scales with concern count
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the model breaks when one change spans several slices, an endpoint plus its migration plus a worker in one review degrades attention until the per-slice checks, transaction scope, rollout order, idempotency keys, silently drop
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this model budgets implementation and review effort for bundle consumers, authoring effort for this corpus document is a separate, rarer workload
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate capacity in slice terms, one mode-classified slice with its REQ-WEB rows, layer design, and matrix-assigned tests per review unit, splitting anything larger
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the seed's 25-endpoint ceiling is generous precisely because slices amortize, a service whose endpoints share one harness, one wiring point, and one persistence module reviews far cheaper per endpoint than the first endpoint did

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed measures document properties like label preservation while the shipped service's own reliability questions go unstated, does every workflow have one transaction owner, every repeatable write an idempotency definition, every remote call a timeout policy, and every schema change a rollback that still works
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the bundle's rules define measurable targets directly, the one-owner rule implies zero ambiguous multi-write workflows, the idempotency rules imply zero undefined replay states, the client contract implies zero unclassified remote failures, and the sequencing rules imply zero irreversible rollout steps
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: targets measured only in tests miss the ambiguity failures the security sibling's checklist names, a timeout or crash that leaves a workflow in an undefined state passes every deterministic test and fails only in production timing
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: targets here cover service correctness and delivery safety, latency SLOs are the performance section's subject and product uptime belongs to operations
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the operational targets, zero unowned transactions, zero undefined idempotency boundaries on repeatable writes, zero unclassified remote failure paths, and a working rollback after every rollout step
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that all four targets are greppable or reviewable before deployment, transaction owners, idempotency keys, failure-class matches, and rollback notes are static artifacts, the discipline converts reliability from observation into reviewable structure

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers document-verification retries but not the runtime retry surfaces this theme owns, failure-class-specific policies at remote boundaries, durable retries behind workers, and idempotency keys that make retries safe to receive
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the security sibling composes these into a ladder, classify the failure first, client error, server error, timeout, transport failure, malformed response, then assign each class its policy, fail fast, retry, record for replay, surface to operator, or move to async recovery
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: retrying without classification is the ladder's collapse, a client error retried burns quota on a request that can never succeed, and a timeout retried without an idempotency key may execute the side-effect twice
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this section governs service-level retry and backpressure behavior, corpus-process retries stay in the seed bullets, and client-side UI retry belongs to frontend themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the runtime ladder, classify by failure class, retry only the retryable classes, key every repeatable write, and move durable retries behind the worker boundary section 6 defines
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that idempotency is backpressure's receiving end, the sibling's four definitions, key boundary, replay state, sameness, and concurrency behavior, are what let a service absorb the retry storms its own timeouts provoke, senders and receivers of retries are designed as one system

Bad: a blanket three-retries policy applied to malformed responses. Borderline: infinite worker retries on an operator-visible queue, defensible with alerting, unbounded without it

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed logs document-usage evidence and generic counters but not the backend-specific signals the bundle makes observable, correlation identifiers on every request, worker state transitions operators can see, readiness distinct from liveness, and secrets provably absent from logs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the ops sibling demands structured tracing with propagated identifiers and health surfaces that reflect real dependencies, and the playbook's split definitions require operator-visible state transitions, so the checklist items are transcriptions of stated bundle requirements
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: observability that stops at error counts cannot answer the checklist's own triage questions, without correlation identifiers a multi-layer failure cannot be walked back to its owning layer, and the five-layer anatomy loses its diagnostic value
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this checklist specifies observability of backend service behavior, business analytics and frontend telemetry belong to their own systems
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the minimal service record, correlated structured traces per request, worker state transitions per workflow, readiness and liveness split per the ops sibling, and a secret-redaction check in review
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the checklist's cheapest item carries the most weight, propagating one request identifier through all five layers turns the anatomy into a queryable index, every incident becomes a filtered trace instead of a log excavation

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed sets p95 and p99 ceilings while the bundle defines the mechanism-level method, verify boundary behavior first, pool and client reuse, transaction scope, inline-versus-worker placement, because those mechanisms are where backend latency regressions originate
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the playbook's rules are performance rules in disguise, per-request client construction adds connection setup to every call, transactions spanning remote calls serialize the pool, and inline fan-out holds connections open, so mechanism audit explains what latency numbers only report
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: verifying only the ceiling invites the wrong fix, a slow endpoint gets caching sprinkled over it when the actual defect is a transaction held across a remote call that no cache can shorten
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this method verifies service-level request performance, database query tuning and infrastructure sizing belong to their own methods
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to measure mechanism first, client reuse, transaction span, executor blocking, and work placement, then confirm the seed's ceilings as the user-facing consequence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the seed's own precondition is the method's sharpest rule, require a service-specific SLO before deployment and document when latency does not apply, making absent SLOs a named gap rather than an implicit pass
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to audit the four mechanisms on the changed path, then measure p95 and p99 on representative handlers against the SLO or the seed's fallback ceilings
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the playbook's rules are performance rules in disguise, per-request client construction adds connection setup to every call, transactions spanning remote calls serialize the pool, and inline fan-out holds connections open, so mechanism audit explains what latency numbers only report
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; verifying only the ceiling invites the wrong fix, a slow endpoint gets caching sprinkled over it when the actual defect is a transaction held across a remote call that no cache can shorten

- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: measure mechanism first, client reuse, transaction span, executor blocking, and work placement, then confirm the seed's ceilings as the user-facing consequence

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bounds document scale but not the discipline's scaling seams, the traffic level where inline work must move behind workers, the instance count where zero-downtime sequencing becomes mandatory, and the service count where this single-service anatomy stops describing the system
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the bundle states two seams directly, section 6 flips inline to durable when retries, fan-out, or held connections appear, and the ops sibling makes the four-step schema evolution the default whenever multiple instances or staggered rollouts are possible, the third seam, multi-service architecture, is the seed's own stated stop line
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: scaling by stretching the existing shapes defeats them, an inline handler absorbing tenfold traffic becomes a connection-holding retry amplifier, and a single-instance migration habit under rolling deploys ships the impossible orderings the sibling forbids
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this statement marks where this theme's single-service guidance stops, cross-service contracts, distributed sagas, and platform architecture are out of scope
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the seams, traffic growth re-triggers the section 6 criteria, instance growth mandates the four-step evolution pattern, and service multiplication exits this theme entirely
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that all three seams share one shape, assumptions that were invisible at small scale, short requests, single instances, one service, become load-bearing exactly when growth invalidates them, so the seams are best checked at growth events, not on a calendar
